Finally, I brush my hair left and right, while avoid touching my scalp at all, then brush it toward the front, the point from doing that is to spread the product around with my dry hair so it's not as greasy only on one area.<br />At night, I just rub the product in with my fingers, or repeat the day time routine if I have to see people. This extreme hair loss lasted for about six to eight weeks for me and was very dramatic for the first four or five weeks before gradually slowing down and virtually stopping altogether. After five or six weeks I started noticing new thin hairs on my temples, hands, back, etc. I'm sure I was also growing some on my scalp, but they just weren't as visible as the others. It took over three months before I felt as though I'd grown most of the hair I'd lost during the initial shedding back. I stopped using this product before I'd grown much new hair so I can't say for sure if it worked really well, but I can say that it at least worked a little. The one thing I will say is that for anyone who has only a little bit of hair loss, this 5% solution is pretty intense and probably not the right choice. If you're not ready for the side effects you should not use it because your hair will eventually become dependent upon it.<br /><br />These side effects include drowsiness, itching, dandruff and of course the initial shedding. I think I've already covered the dandruff and initial shedding. The drowsiness is pretty intense for the first two or three weeks and then comes and goes in spurts after that. I began taking 5 Hour Energy almost daily during the work week, but after about the 10 week mark I didn't need the energy boost as much and only took 5 Hour Energy once or twicea week as needed. It became manageable when I planned my day around the drowsy burst. The itching was very bad during the shedding period. After that it continued, but could be ignored for most of the day. I think if I'd continued to use this 5% solution long enough the itching would have eventually become a non-issue.<br /><br />One other thing that I've experienced with both the 5% and 2% solution is a feeling like liquid is sliding around just underneath my scalp. I don't know if this means that I'm using too much or what, but even when I don't experience itching I do feel this. All in all, the product did prove to regrow hair. The side effects of this particular product were too much for me though. Also, make sure you get the unscented version. I accidently got a scented version of the 2% solution and the odor it gave off was horrible beyond description. I may just have had a bad reaction to it, but even if it is 10% of that for you it will not be something you want to experience. Better safe than sorry. I have never had any problems with odors on the unscented version of this product.

Try washing your hair with different kinds of soap instead of shampoo if you have problems with dandruff.<br /><br />Application can be tricky in the beginning, but you get the routine going. In the evening I just apply right before going to bed as there is no risk of it running down my face while lying down. In the morning I massage it into the scalp. Massaging should not be necessary, but it is a good way to get it everywhere without it dripping to much. Then I use some paper to remove the excess liquid from the hair as it otherwise will form a white layer as it dries. Paper consumption has gone up a lot and I am keeping a short hairstyle as that makes application easier. The morning routine takes about 3 minutes once you get it going. I plan to continue using this product.

  250. My hairline began to recede in my late teens, and the hair on the top of my head started to thin soon thereafter. Right before I turned 21, the thinning drastically accelerated. I was noticeably thin on top, but it wasn't too bad if I kept the sides and back short and textured (having a good hair stylist is important!) Around 23 I tried Lipogaine, but I didn't care for the dropper or the oily feeling. After my 24th birthday passed this May, and many more hairs graced the floor of my shower, I decided to take action.<br /><br />In June 2013, I purchased a 6 month supply of Kirkland brand minoxidil foam along with a bottle of PerfectHAIR shampoo (the shampoo was supposed to be only a 30 day supply, but I've been using the same bottle daily for over three months and still have some remaining.) I use the shampoo each morning in the shower and let it sit for about five minutes. After my hair finishes soaking, I rinse and dry with a blow dryer once I'm out of the shower. Once dried off, I apply the suggested amount of minoxidil foam to my scalp and massage it in. I don't use any hair products -- the foam is my styling mousse. Then at the end of the day, about an hour before I go to bed, I apply one more round of foam and massage it in. The foam works well enough like a mousse, but it dissolves quickly so work fast.<br /><br />Nearly four months and a short haircut later (I usually wear it long), I'm pleased to say that I've significantly regrown hair on the top of my head in addition to a good deal of hairline. I know this product isn't intended to regrow your hairline, let alone guaranteed to regrow any hair at all, but it worked out for me. I'm no longer noticeably thin on top, and I've regained a good amount of hair along my temples, so I no longer have as bad of an \\"island.\\"<br /><br />The first month was slow and tedious, but I was soon able to see little hairs sprouting on my hairline. Around the second month, the hairs were noticeably longer and darkerand I observed that I couldn't see as much scalp on top as before. After the second and half month, I decided to shave my head from about 5 inches on top and 3 inches on the sides / back, to a no. 5 with clippers so I could see my progress. I am truly amazed with the results.<br /><br />I definitely recommend using this product in conjunction with the PerfectHAIR if your hair is starting to thin. I'm very thankful that my body reacted to the minoxidil and shampoo, and I'm pretty sure that I wouldn't have achieved results like this if I had waited a while longer -- the sooner you start, the better! Keep in mind that you won't notice much at first because it takes time to grow new hair. Also, hair grows only about half an inch per month, so I think 3 months is a good waiting period to give yourself before you see results. Depending on how you wear your hair, your progress may not be as noticeable. I usually keep my hair at a medium length, but I really didn't notice how much hair I had regrown until I shaved my head to even out the longer hairs with the shorter new ones.<br /><br />The next experiment will be to see how long these new hairs grow!<br /><br />Good luck everyone!

  306. A lot of people have negative things to say about Minoxidil, (or Rogaine) – the truth is topical hair serums/gels have limited scope in terms of who it will work for. For one, this product won’t grow your hair back if you are bad, its more of a preventative measure to keep your hair from thinning. Second, this product will NOT work overnight. Once you start using this product, you will continue to shed for weeks. This does not mean you should stop using it, a lot of people will write negative reviews about this product because it’s not an instant fix. Please don’t give up hope so quickly, it may work for you it just takes time. Lastly, there’s a difference in the causes of hair loss. Some hair loss is caused by genetics (more than half of all cases), and in this case, you’ll need to try products like this Minoxidil, or go even further and get plugs. However, some cases for hair thinning might have nothing to do with your genes, but rather vitamin deficiencies or an improper diet. In these circumstances, supplementing your diet with [[ASIN:B00S8H9IVY A Biotin formulated for hair regrowth]] like this one would be a good bet. The goal for me was to identified exactly what the root cause of my hair loss was, in order for me to know what measures I should take to stop my hair loss. I take both the biotin and Minoxidil for good measure, and I’ve been seeing encouraging results so far.<br /><br />The vertex of my hairline (where I’ve been seeing the most change) is the area that I’m the most concerned about, and I can say that using these products has slowed down the rate of decline. My father has the same issue as me, and he said at my age he had a lot less hair. I don’t know if that statement is encouraging or not, but at least it means that something is working.<br /><br />I’ll continue to use these products until more drastic measures are necessary.

  538. It's been a long time ago, when I started to lose hair - in summer 1996! It took several months, until I realized that I was not paranoid, but then I immediately visited a doctor, who recommended me an anti-androgen topical called Alpicort F. It was a good stuff; I didn't regrow any hair, but it was very reliable for maintenance. In the spring 1999, I started to apply 2% minoxidil in some bald areas in my temples, and it produced some mild regrowth of vellus hair. Hence I switched to 2% minoxidil. In the summer 2008, I found out that cheap generic forms of Rogaine became available, and I switched to 5%Kirkland minoxidil. To my surprise, it produced some very mild regrowth of hair in my temples. Apparently, the effectiveness of minoxidil increases with increasing dosage. It is true that I observed some dandruff during the first weeks of use, but after ca. 2 months it eventually disappeared.<br /><br />I must stress that during this time, I haven't lost any hair (or at least, I couldn't notice any loss in my temples). And I applied it only once a day. I think that minoxidil is great as a sort of prevention, and at least in my case, it didn't lose effectiveness over time. For some people, the 5% version may be too weak. For me, stronger versions of minoxidil are too strong and damage my hair. I think that it is because I am a very good responder to this stuff. In 2011, I was experimenting with 15% minoxidil versions in thinned areas of my temples and it turned out to be a big mistake. It caused a quick telogen effluvium in me, it didn't regrow any appreciable amount of hair, and what is worse, my hair became dependent on this concentration. After I quitted it, I started to shed very rapidly and my hair was virtually annihilated everywhere, where I had applied it. It has never regrown again. Since that time I have been trying to get it back (but that's another story). I think that it is always better to combine 5% minoxidil with some DHT-blocker, rather than risking theRussian roulette with 10-15% minoxidil.<br /><br />NOTE: I routinely order Kirkland minoxidil from their internet website, but recently, I was surprised that CostCo changed the manufacturer (for PERRIGO in Israel) and the bottles look differently. Some customers already shared their experience with this minoxidil that was not too positive. I have been taking it for one month only, so it's not possible to evaluate its effictiveness yet, but I would be curious, what other people say. After 16 years of minoxidil use, all my scalp is already latently affected by DHT, and if I started to use some less effective stuff, I would lose all my hair at once.

  619. Like my father and maternal grandfather I started losing my hair in my late 20s, right around the time Minoxidil came on the market. No knock on either of them, but I'm vain and didn't want to look old before my time. I started on the original 2% solution back in the early 1990s and was VERY pleased with the results. While using Minoxidil didn't stop my hair loss dead in its tracks it certainly did arrest it and it works on my specific type of hair loss (on the crown of my head or male pattern baldness). The hair that remained looked perfectly normal and it was augmented by very light colored short sort of downy hair that grew in. It kept my scalp from getting the shiny bald look so I chalked it up as a win. After using Minoxidil for 20 years now I have the hairline my dad had at 30, which isn't bad considering I'm coming up on 50. Is it a thick lush head of hair? No, but it's not a shiny cue ball either. I do know that the 5% solution netted better results for me than the 2% solution so if you're going to get in, go ALL in. And as someone who's used it for 20 years I can tell you that no, your barber or stylist won't know you use it, no one will unless you tell them. I've never had any side effects either. I'm sure results can and do vary and like most men I'm too vain to mention it to most friends so maybe you have others who are using it as well and don't know. If you're looking to start you can't beat the deal on this 6 month supply of Minoxidil. Does it last six months? Absolutely! I've used other generics like Members Mark (sold at Sam's Club) and there's really no difference between the brand name (Rogaine) and the generics.<br /><br />So far it sounds all good right? Well, there are some things that people undoubtedly will not like. Applying the solution with the eyedropper can be messy and it does dribble down the side of your head to places where you don't want/need it. The early kits had a sprayer, but the problem was it would get on your hair rather than your scalp. A dabber type instrument used to be included but my hunch/worry was that it wound up damaging the remaining hair follicles worse than the help that was arriving. Slow and steady with applying the solution is the rule, or use your fingers to assist, however be CERTAIN to wash your hands immediately as you do NOT want this getting in your eyes! Trust me on that! The other minor complaint is that once applied it is slow to dry, giving you a wet hair look that isn't uniformly wet like you've come out of the shower. But you know what? I've never had someone ask me \\"why is your hair still wet?\\" Trust me...most people are too polite to ask questions that genuinely puzzle them. I've read about issues with clumping and other oddities and that does happen if you have relatively thick hair. Once it dries some gently brush or comb your hair. From time to time I've had residue that remains on my scalp but it washes off when you shower next. Some users get irritation or burning; if that happens stop using it or see a doctor.<br /><br />Granted, this product isn't for everyone. Some don't like the idea of applying twice a day, don't like the wet hair look that's slow to dry, or expect immediate visible results. Minoxidil isn't a sprint, it's a marathon and take it from someone who's been running that marathon for 20 years, it's ultimately worth it. I love my dad and know what I'd look like at 50 if I hadn't been using Minoxidil and am glad I've been using it as I think I look more youthful and vibrant. Most people don't guess my actual age in fact. I can't give Minoxidil all the credit on that, but it sure helps; maybe it can help you too!ur hair rather than your scalp.   851. The active ingredient in both this Kirkland brand and in the Rogaine brand is the same, which is Minoxidil. For those of you who don’t know, this recently came off-patent so anyone can use the same active ingredient, allowing companies like Costco (Kirkland) to sell cheaper versions of the same product. That said, you should really only use this product if you already know [[ASIN:B0000Y8H3S this product, Rogaine]] is going to work for you. There seems to be two types of people who have baldness –those who Minoxidil works for, and those who it does not. This is why you’ll see so many 1 star reviews for Rogaine or this Kirkland Minoxidil. Honestly they are very similar, you might notice some lower quality in Monoxidil by Kirkland in terms of foaming-effect but they have the same ingredient and I’ve found the work equally as well.<br /><br />There are other products you can try if you find that Minoxidil doesn’t work for you, such as a [[ASIN:B00KYXSF00 Biochanin-A product like this one]]. It affects the hair in a different way than Minoxidil. Minoxidil tries to make your body circulate more blood to your scalp where your follicles will grow. A Biochanin A product works at inhibiting the chemicals our body produces that lead to hair loss. Both approaches are equally valid, except some work for some, and other’s work for others. If you’re like me, you’ve probably tried both. I can say that the Biochanin A product from NuNutrients has been the most effective for me in-terms of seeing hair regrowth, but I’ve also used Rogaine as well as the Kirkland brand and seen results, just a lot slower.

This supply is a Cosco brand, and also made in Israel. I didn't see much difference with either country of origin. I usually burn for sure if I forget. But alas, I did not burn my usual bald spot. Now out 9 months and my barber says that I have decent regrowth and \\"mirrored it\\" for me to see. Yippie!!<br />Side Effects - I can attest that for me, the side effects are minimal, dandruff being the only one I suffer from. I have not had the itching that others have reported, but I do have dandruff now (that I never had before) that seems cyclic. For a few days it's not too bad, but then one day I will shed like crazy. I just run a fine tooth comb through the hair and try and get out as much as I can. I have been using an alternating method of Head and Shoulders and Selsun Blue daily since the first use because of reviews I've read. So I'm not sure that if I stop using these two shampoos if I would have better or worse dandruff. At some point I may let the shampoo's run out and see how I do. I would give 5 stars if not for the slight trade off.<br />Usage - You most definitely need to use this EVERY day TWICE a day for the REST OF YOUR LIFE. If you're unwilling to commit, then pass. Most reviews will have people state that they \\"tried it but didn't see any relief\\" (but for how long?) or \\"I use it only once a day\\" (not as directed) or \\"I only use .75ml at a time\\" (again, not directed). You need to apply following the directions and you need to be diligent. You can have the occasional miss dose here and there, but don't slack, keep on it. I use 1ml TWICE a day, massaged into the hair and scalp at the crown by using a cross pattern. I really work it in. I try not to get my hair \\"re-wet\\" (pool swimming, etc.) until about three hours after application.<br />All in all, your results may vary, I'm happy!
